<div id="review_132611072" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/132611072" />
    <a title="Morgan F" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2941288-morgan-f"><img alt="Morgan F" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1262298598p2/2941288.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/132611072?book_show_action=true">Nov 27, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Morgan F" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Morgan F" href="/user/show/2941288-morgan-f">Morgan F</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780385737630" href="/book/show/7558747-revolution">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2941288-morgan-f?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2941288-morgan-f?shelf=grief">grief</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2941288-morgan-f?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2941288-morgan-f?shelf=music">music</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2941288-morgan-f?shelf=pretty-covers">pretty-covers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2941288-morgan-f?shelf=good-sized">good-sized</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2941288-morgan-f?shelf=read-2010">read-2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2941288-morgan-f?shelf=its-a-girl">its-a-girl</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2941288-morgan-f?shelf=2010">2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2941288-morgan-f?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer132611072" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3334451683296559472">Andi Alpers, a troubled Brooklyn teen, is always one step away from the edge. The only thing keeping her going over is her love of music, but even that doesn't seem enough at times. Two years ago her younger brother, the glue keeping her family together, died. Now her mother, a talented French painter, is suffering from a psychotic break down, and her father, a workaholic scientist, refuses to acknowledge his old family while he lives a new life. Andi is content with flunking out of her prestigi</span>
  <span id="freeText3334451683296559472" style="display:none">Andi Alpers, a troubled Brooklyn teen, is always one step away from the edge. The only thing keeping her going over is her love of music, but even that doesn't seem enough at times. Two years ago her younger brother, the glue keeping her family together, died. Now her mother, a talented French painter, is suffering from a psychotic break down, and her father, a workaholic scientist, refuses to acknowledge his old family while he lives a new life. Andi is content with flunking out of her prestigious liberal high school, but her father, in a rare burst of parental concern, forces her to come with him to Paris so she can focus on working on a project that might save her grade. Her father is called to Paris because a colleague of his, a famous historian, needs his help in identifying a shriveled up heart encased in crystal that might just belong to the young Louis XVII, the son of King Louis XVI, who was guillotined in the French Revolution. While shifting through some artifacts, Andi discovers the long-hidden journal of Alexandrine, an aspiring actress and companion to young Louis, who is struggling to save herself and her charge. Whilst reading this diary, the fates of the two young women are woven together, and Andi will come to discover that internal revolutions are just as affecting as external ones. <br /><br />I loved this book. It was lovely. The writing was beautiful, lyrical, and intricate. Andi was intriguing and relatable. Sometimes her constant negative attitude, especially towards the beginning, could become bothersome, but she was extremely interesting. Her sarcastic comments were often funny, and she had a lot going on underneath the surface. Her feelings, as well as her love for music, seemed to transcend the page. I loved Alexandrine too. Although she was in the book less than Andi, her role in it was just as vital. One thing I loved about this story was how everything connected. I could mentally see the puzzle pieces coming together, and it was a thrill to watch everything unfold. Also, I learned a buttload about the French Revolution, but it never seemed like I was reading a text book. I can tell Ms. Donnelly did her research, and it was very in-depth and well-done. <br /><br />The only thing I did not like were the hints of the supernatural. To explain myself without giving away to much of the plot, I will say that this book is a lot like the movie Happy Feet. I do not mean to allude that there were dancing penguins in the streets of Paris. But, you know how towards the end of the movie, the plot does a complete 360, and the film is no longer about cute tap-dancing birds, but rather some heavy-handed environmental message? This book is kind of like that. Towards the end, it took a really sharp turn, and I'm not sure whether what happened was real or not. I mean, I guess it worked, but it shook me out of the story for a little bit. That's what kept me from giving this novel 5 stars. <br /><br />Anyway, I recommend this book. I recommend it to fans of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/64481.A_Northern_Light" title="A Northern Light by Jennifer Donnelly" rel="nofollow noopener">A Northern Light</a>. I recommend it to fans of historical-fiction. I recommend it to those interested in a more personal look at the French Revolution. I recommend it to music lovers. And I recommend it for anyone looking for a satisfying, thought-provoking read. <br /><br />An awesome read that will stay with me. I have a feeling it will help me when my history class studies the French Revolution next month. </span>
  <a data-text-id="3334451683296559472" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_136281097" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/136281097" />
    <a title="Lisa Vegan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/83445-lisa-vegan"><img alt="Lisa Vegan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1243394822p2/83445.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/136281097?book_show_action=true">Dec 23, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lisa Vegan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lisa Vegan" href="/user/show/83445-lisa-vegan">Lisa Vegan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780385737630" href="/book/show/7558747-revolution">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">all historical fiction fans; those who have a fascination with the guillotine (which I don’t but…)</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/83445-lisa-vegan?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/83445-lisa-vegan?shelf=novel">novel</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/83445-lisa-vegan?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/83445-lisa-vegan?shelf=groups-buddies">groups-buddies</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/83445-lisa-vegan?shelf=books-about-books">books-about-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/83445-lisa-vegan?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/83445-lisa-vegan?shelf=readbooks-female-author-or-illust">readbooks-female-author-or-illust</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/83445-lisa-vegan?shelf=z2011">z2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/83445-lisa-vegan?shelf=zz-4star">zz-4star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/83445-lisa-vegan?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer136281097" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15582782765452842701">Wow! This story, two intertwining stories actually, was very effective storytelling. It was a fabulous way to tell a historical fiction story.<br/><br/>It’s about two young women in their late teens, Andi who’s living in the 21st century and Alex who’s living in the 18th century, during the time of the French Revolution. We learn about Alex as Andi is reading her diary.<br/><br/>Does every main character in young adult books have to be extraordinary to be interesting to the reader?! When I first started this, that </span>
  <span id="freeText15582782765452842701" style="display:none">Wow! This story, two intertwining stories actually, was very effective storytelling. It was a fabulous way to tell a historical fiction story.<br /><br />It’s about two young women in their late teens, Andi who’s living in the 21st century and Alex who’s living in the 18th century, during the time of the French Revolution. We learn about Alex as Andi is reading her diary.<br /><br />Does every main character in young adult books have to be extraordinary to be interesting to the reader?! When I first started this, that was my gripe. But, I like that Andi, who lives in Brooklyn, New York, has a genius level IQ, is an accomplished musician, speaks French fluently, is well educated, and independent and resolute, knowing her own mind, is willing to work hard, and is also seriously depressed and grieving. I’m assuming her psychotropic medication was helping her depression enough so she could function as well as she did.<br /><br />Alex’s story is also fascinating. Through it I learned quite a bit about the French Revolution. (I am not as well educated as Andi, it seems.) Though fictionalized, of course, I got a wonderful and slightly different perspective on Marie Antoinette. When I was back in the 18th century, everything was just as vivid as in the other story/today’s world. Anybody who has any fascination with guillotining will get their fill here; those descriptions were quite vivid.<br /><br />The stories are psychologically sophisticated about depression, human relationships, and human nature too.<br /><br />I did guess the “mystery” that’s a part of this book, and fairly early on, but that did not at all detract from my enjoyment of the book. The entire story was gripping; as I read on &amp; on, it got harder &amp; harder to put down the book.<br /><br />In addition to Andi and Alex, music (and a variety at that!) is another main character that shines in this book. I love how the author was able to incorporate music (musicians, instruments, specific pieces and songs, and music’s importance) throughout the entire book. She did it brilliantly. There were also at least a dozen other characters that were wonderfully presented.<br /><br />I cared about Andi and Alex and most of the other characters too. I got very invested in them. At one of the saddest moments, capable of sending the reader (along with the main character) into utter despair, I got one of the biggest laughs from the book; that was an amazing feat. It did not at all feel manipulative, but rather true to life.<br /><br />At first I wasn’t so sure I liked a long portion toward the end, but I ended up loving it. While open to interpretation, I enjoyed my take on it and I think it’s the one that’s meant to be taken; I’m happy with how I understand that part of the plot. For some time I was afraid this would totally disintegrate into a pedestrian teenage love story, but I was pleasantly surprised.<br /><br />There are quite a few notable quotes in this book. I added at least one to my quotes and could have added several. There is (for me) a powerful message about how healing oneself can often best be accomplished by being there for and helping someone else.<br /><br />The notes on sources and bibliography at the end of the book are sufficiently extensive that it’s obvious how much research went into writing this book, as much as for many non-fiction books. It showed!<br /><br />4 ½ stars<br /><br />Edited to add: This author is able to describe and write about depression remarkably well!</span>
  <a data-text-id="15582782765452842701" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_574975567" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/574975567" />
    <a title="Aoibhínn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5799885-aoibh-nn"><img alt="Aoibhínn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1452957222p2/5799885.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/574975567?book_show_action=true">Mar 29, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aoibhínn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aoibhínn" href="/user/show/5799885-aoibh-nn">Aoibhínn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781408801512" href="/book/show/11743055-revolution">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5799885-aoibh-nn?shelf=physical-books">physical-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5799885-aoibh-nn?shelf=bad-awful-books">bad-awful-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5799885-aoibh-nn?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5799885-aoibh-nn?shelf=2013">2013</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer574975567" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4130335669724686387">Andi is broken. She is failing school and failing life. Since the death of her brother, all she cares about is music. Taken to Paris by her estranged father, she makes a discovery there that could transform everything. Hidden in the compartment of an old guitar case is a lost diary from Revolutionary France. <br/><br/>After reading <i>The Tea Rose</i> by Jennifer Donnelly and absolutely loving it, I decided to read another one of her books. I had high expectations with this book. I thought the synopsis on the ba</span>
  <span id="freeText4130335669724686387" style="display:none">Andi is broken. She is failing school and failing life. Since the death of her brother, all she cares about is music. Taken to Paris by her estranged father, she makes a discovery there that could transform everything. Hidden in the compartment of an old guitar case is a lost diary from Revolutionary France. <br /><br />After reading <i>The Tea Rose</i> by Jennifer Donnelly and absolutely loving it, I decided to read another one of her books. I had high expectations with this book. I thought the synopsis on the back of this novel sounded interesting but as soon as I was introduced to suicidal Andi and her obnoxious drug addicted friends I knew I was in for a long read! Around page 60 or so the novel moved to Paris. I thought things would pick up then but I was wrong. There was just another hundred pages of Andi moaning about how her life was so unfair. Sigh. Then we got to Alexandrine's diary entries. These were interesting at first but soon they became tedious and annoying. Alexandrine's narrative sounded far too modern for someone who lived during the 1790's should have sounded. Alexandrine and the other 18th Century characters dialogue just sounded so forced and wrong and the diary entries were so boring! At times during the diary entries it felt like I was reading a history text book rather than a fiction novel. The last 100 pages of this novel were completely absurd and far-fetched. The time travelling twist in the plot was very confusing and irritating. Was it all in Andi's head due to the amount of drugs she's been taking? Or is this a time-travel novel? I had no idea! It was such an abrupt and strange shift in the plot. I honestly think the author must have been high on drugs herself when she wrote this part of the book. <br /><br />The novel was very depressing and it wasn't particularly well-written either. I didn't enjoy it at all. Finishing this novel was torturous. The only reason I finished this novel was for a couple of reading challenges I'm doing. If not for that I would have threw the book away. The only good thing I can say about it is that it was well-researched. The author obviously spent a lot of time researching Music and the French Revolution. <br /><br />None of the characters in this book were very well developed. The main character of Andi was so extremely unlikeable that I didn't care whether she lived or died. I prefer strong female characters in the novels I read. Andi was just far too weak and whiny. She was just a nasty, selfish, stupid, anti-social, spoiled bitch. The supporting characters weren’t much better either. I really didn't like any of them. They were all one dimensional and flat. <br /><br />In the acknowledgments at the end of the book the author thanks her mother for stopping her from throwing the first draft of this novel into a lake. I think that was bad parenting! I don't know how this awful book managed to get passed the editing stage and get published at all. It really is truly terrible. Don't bother reading it. You'll only regret it. <br /><br /><b>One Star!</b><br /><br /><br /><b>NOTE:</b> This is a YA novel but I’d worry about teenagers reading this novel with the main character Andi popping pills like they were M&amp;M’s and the author almost makes suicide sound romantic in this book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4130335669724686387" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_125436613" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/125436613" />
    <a title="Misha Mathew" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3809685-misha-mathew"><img alt="Misha Mathew" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1388910909p2/3809685.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/125436613?book_show_action=true">Oct 09, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Misha Mathew" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Misha Mathew" href="/user/show/3809685-misha-mathew">Misha Mathew</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781408810453" href="/book/show/8665184-revolution">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3809685-misha-mathew?shelf=history">history</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3809685-misha-mathew?shelf=france">france</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3809685-misha-mathew?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3809685-misha-mathew?shelf=books-about-books">books-about-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer125436613" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11764060755140414259">This is the sort of book that makes me go "WOW!" In fact Revolution is one of the 2 books this year, that left me speechless.<br/><br/>Being a book lover , I have liked some books, loved some of them. Every now and then comes along a book that makes me realize why I love reading so much. Revolution , for me , is that sort of a book.<br/><br/>Revolution is about two young girls, living two centuries apart - Andi and Alexandrine.Andi is a high school senior at a super exclusive school. On the surface she has a perfec</span>
  <span id="freeText11764060755140414259" style="display:none">This is the sort of book that makes me go "WOW!" In fact Revolution is one of the 2 books this year, that left me speechless.<br /><br />Being a book lover , I have liked some books, loved some of them. Every now and then comes along a book that makes me realize why I love reading so much. Revolution , for me , is that sort of a book.<br /><br />Revolution is about two young girls, living two centuries apart - Andi and Alexandrine.Andi is a high school senior at a super exclusive school. On the surface she has a perfect life - money, world-famous father, life of comfort and wealth. But the reality is different. She is still tortured by the guilt of having been responsible for her brother's death.<br /><br />Alexandrine, on the other hand, is living in the time of the French Revolution, one of the bloodiest , most violent times in French history. She is a spy and living on the tenterhook of danger.<br /><br />When Andi discovers Alexandrine's diary, it starts a journey to self-revelation.<br />It doesn't take long to realize that the "revolution" described is not the French revolution , despite it playing a major role in the story. The revolution is about changing oneself, its about self-discovery (see the quote below).<br /><br />Andi's only comfort is music. Its through the music that she discovers the diary. And thus starts the "revolution , as two lost young girls , living two hundred years apart connect through music and the words in the diary.<br /><br />The description of music, its beauty and the effect it has on Andi is breathtaking. I like music but have never been so passionate about it. But while reading this book, I could almost feel the emotional and spiritual connection that Andi had with music.<br /><br />The writing is absolutely beautiful. It made the story, the characters , the setting come alive.When a book has paragraphs and more paragraphs, lines and more lines, that I can read and re-read and even remember , that's when I know that the book is going to stay with me. And believe me, Donnelly's writing guarantees that you will go back and re-read some lines again and again. Yet everytime you read it, they will still touch you and move you the same way.<br /><br />I felt so deeply for both the characters. I got so deeply involved - I could feel their fear, hurt , pain.<br />I was blown away by the details and description of the French Revolution. Jennifer Donnelly truly makes history come alive with powerful words that makes the reader feel the horror, see the violence unfolding in front of their eyes. I can imagine the amount of research and work that must have gone into not only the details of the French Revolution , but also the music.<br /><br />One of the most powerful points that this book makes is that its never too late to discover oneself, its never too late for anything, no matter how much life lets you down. <br /><br />Revolution is incredibly sad and yet incredibly beautiful. Despite the grim atmosphere throughout the book, there is also hope and optimism -there is always a ray of sunshine at the end of the storm.<br /><br />I had a major test the next day and I am usually obsessively cautious about avoiding the last minute panic. But while I read this book, I actually forgot about the test and yet didn't regret it a bit.<br /><br />There are not enough words to describe this book. Just read it and find it out yourself. <br />Revolution is an unforgettable book totally worth your time.<br /><br />Favorite Quote:<br />"Life’s all about the revolution, isn’t it? The one inside, I mean. You can’t change history. You can’t change the world. All you can ever change is yourself." <br /><br />Overall:<br />Revolution is an exquisitely written book that is worth reading and remembering.<br /><br />Recommended?<br />Yes! To every person , no matter genre you read.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11764060755140414259" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_337465468" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/337465468" />
    <a title="Parvathy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4915009-parvathy"><img alt="Parvathy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1425840439p2/4915009.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/337465468?book_show_action=true">May 27, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Parvathy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Parvathy" href="/user/show/4915009-parvathy">Parvathy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780385737630" href="/book/show/7558747-revolution">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">History lovers</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4915009-parvathy?shelf=confused">confused</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4915009-parvathy?shelf=informative">informative</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4915009-parvathy?shelf=fantasy-politics">fantasy-politics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4915009-parvathy?shelf=strong-females">strong-females</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4915009-parvathy?shelf=historicals">historicals</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4915009-parvathy?shelf=movie-material">movie-material</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4915009-parvathy?shelf=past-lives">past-lives</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4915009-parvathy?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4915009-parvathy?shelf=thought-provoking">thought-provoking</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4915009-parvathy?shelf=broken-characters">broken-characters</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer337465468" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer606831891917111386"><b>4.5 stars</b><br/><br/> <b>Someone</b> once told me that people tend to like tragedy more than happily ever after stories because it is more realistic. That got me thinking Was it true? Are we really satisfied when a book or a story ends in tragedy? When the guy doesn't get the girl or when things end in the worst possible way. Think about Shakespeare. He is more famous for his classics like Romeo and Juliet, Hamlet, Macbeth, Othello and King Lear than his As you like it, All is well that ends well and many of his o</span>
  <span id="freeText606831891917111386" style="display:none"><b>4.5 stars</b><br /><br /> <b>Someone</b> once told me that people tend to like tragedy more than happily ever after stories because it is more realistic. That got me thinking Was it true? Are we really satisfied when a book or a story ends in tragedy? When the guy doesn't get the girl or when things end in the worst possible way. Think about Shakespeare. He is more famous for his classics like Romeo and Juliet, Hamlet, Macbeth, Othello and King Lear than his As you like it, All is well that ends well and many of his other plays were the good defeats evil and the characters have a happy ending. When a book is happy it will not stay with you and torture you for the rest of your life. It gives you fleeting moments of happiness and just fades away into some dark recess of your mind. Tragedy makes you think about what could have gone differently? Tragedy makes you hope, believe that things could have gone differently only if ......<br /><br />So it would come as no surprise that this book which is centred around a very disturbed young women set in a very tragic time in history aka the French revolution managed to impress me. View point is a very curious thing. When you are a lowly clergy you look upon the nobility with their vainness and vanity, as the most despicable, heartless and cruel human beings that has ever walked this earth. Those who dab themselves in perfume and eat out of a silver platter while your family has barely enough to survive, no one could blame them if you decide to rise up. When you are royalty on the other hand, born and raised like one is it surprising that your viewpoint cannot go beyond the four walls that surround you. Are you to be blamed for the way you were raised and for getting the things others don't get. In this book you have a character who is on the verge of ending her life because of a tragedy she could not prevent. She blames herself on the basis of all the "if only's" that she can think of and wish for a different outcome every day. This very same young woman discovers a diary left behind by a girl roughly her same age who lived and died in the year 1795 in the middle of the French revolution which contains details of her acts of defiance for one small child, she loved more than anything whom revolution marked as a pariah and condemned to a tragic death. The child is non other than the Lost King of France Louie X VII and the diary gives an insiders account of the French Revolution from the point of view of the King and his family. See them not as the monarchs that brought about the downfall of France but as a family trying to stay alive and together. Louis-Charles as an innocent 8 year old boy who was born in the wrong family, at the wrong time. Can you fault any of them for there actions? Is their no end to the revolution? Does characters like Robespierre, Hitler, Napoleon or Mussolini bring about revolutions or is it people like us? These are some of the questions raised by the 17 year old girl who keeps an account of her life so that someone would some day find it and see the revolution for what it is and these are the very same questions that lead a 21st century young girl to follow the same path.<br /><br />The level of details and the historical research put forth by the author is outstanding and the bibliography is a testament to the effort put in. I have always liked Jennifer Donnelly's characterisation and writing style. She goes into elaborate details about the world she creates keeping monotony at bay and with just enough material to transport you to that time. Being a fiction book if you ask me to describe it in one word I would say realistic. Not the story itself because there are things in there that seem way to convenient and some that would never happen in the real world but the premise itself is what I like to call realistic, the French Revolution background with the severed heads and the guillotine, the streets and gutters of Paris overflowing with blood, the orphans in the street and women pressing their handkerchiefs to the necks of guillotined victims to make souvenirs, all make for a gruesome and realistic picture of this world which is very hard to get out of your mind. Highly informative and remarkably written this book is one keeper that will earn a spot in your bookshelf. <br /> </span>
  <a data-text-id="606831891917111386" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

<span id="freeTextContainer1326124870500035901">I LOVED this book. The characters were incredible and well fleshed-out, the setting was beautiful, the writing and plot were amazing. <br/><br/>I loved how there were musical references throughout the whole book and they fit perfectly with the rest of the plot. Some authors will try to make references like this and they will stick out of the book like a sore thumb. Nope, everything fit perfectly together.<br/><br/>Andi at the beginning was hard and bitter, essentially a toxic character. However, there was something</span>
  <span id="freeText1326124870500035901" style="display:none">I LOVED this book. The characters were incredible and well fleshed-out, the setting was beautiful, the writing and plot were amazing. <br /><br />I loved how there were musical references throughout the whole book and they fit perfectly with the rest of the plot. Some authors will try to make references like this and they will stick out of the book like a sore thumb. Nope, everything fit perfectly together.<br /><br />Andi at the beginning was hard and bitter, essentially a toxic character. However, there was something about her that just made me love her and relate to her. <br /><br />I loved how faith and ambition (among other things) were discussed and shown through the story. Everything was shown in a way that made you see the bad side of it, when previously you had thought it was good, or helpful, or benign at the very least. This sounds like the book was depressing, but it wasn't. It just gave more perspective.<br /><br />The way history was described, through both Alex's and Andi's eyes, made everything so vivid and real. This parallel story was touching, enlightening, and suspenseful. It made me see and understand so many thing that I has never noticed before.<br /><br />I could say a lot more but i dont know how to say it in words. This book is one of my favorites.</span>

  <span id="freeText2238209101175357366" style="display:none">This book had me at "Hello." Andi's voice was so heartbreaking, so powerfully real, that I was in her world from page one. The melancholy undertone carries through the entire book, even when Andi wasn't thinking about the personal tragedy that decimated her family and her own peace of mind. <br /><br />But while this was at times so sad it brought me to tears, it was ultimately a story of hope, inner strength, and the healing power of love. A story, as Donnelly herself said in an interview, that is "...about the internal revolution. The one inside. The one that we human beings all go through as we try to make sense of our world and of its tragedies.”<br /><br />One of my very favorites of the last 12 months. <br /><br /></span>

<div id="review_1730593947" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1730593947" />
    <a title="lucky little cat" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/38160628-lucky-little-cat"><img alt="lucky little cat" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1600336662p2/38160628.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1730593947?book_show_action=true">Aug 16, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="lucky little cat" class="user" itemprop="url" name="lucky little cat" href="/user/show/38160628-lucky-little-cat">lucky little cat</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38160628-lucky-little-cat?shelf=hey-it-s-ya">hey-it-s-ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38160628-lucky-little-cat?shelf=what-s-the-name-of">what-s-the-name-of</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38160628-lucky-little-cat?shelf=read-in-2020">read-in-2020</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38160628-lucky-little-cat?shelf=historiche">historiche</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38160628-lucky-little-cat?shelf=space-opera-time-travel">space-opera-time-travel</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38160628-lucky-little-cat?shelf=it-s-just-a-fantasy">it-s-just-a-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1730593947" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6311561792574288575">The historical part rocks. But the rest of this Sofia Coppola's <i>Marie Antoinette</i>-era-ish novel doesn't hold up so well to rereading. The present-day narrative makes you go "Hunh? <i>Every</i> adult in Andi's life is mean, clueless or insane with grief?" Yeah, that can happen IRL, but add in that the guitar-playing prodigy is swept unwillingly off to Paris by her mean, old genome-sequencing genius Dad on a work trip where <i>of course</i> she <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[falls in love <a class='jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction'>(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> w/in, like half an hour</span>
  <span id="freeText6311561792574288575" style="display:none">The historical part rocks. But the rest of this Sofia Coppola's <i>Marie Antoinette</i>-era-ish novel doesn't hold up so well to rereading. The present-day narrative makes you go "Hunh? <i>Every</i> adult in Andi's life is mean, clueless or insane with grief?" Yeah, that can happen IRL, but add in that the guitar-playing prodigy is swept unwillingly off to Paris by her mean, old genome-sequencing genius Dad on a work trip where <i>of course</i> she <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[falls in love <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> w/in, like half an hour. <br /><br />Ya just gotta figure Donnelly had fun writing this one and roll with it. </span>
  <a data-text-id="6311561792574288575" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_review_1730593947'><a id="like_count_review_1730593947" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/1730593947?resource_type=Review"><span class="likesCount">8 likes</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it gr-button gr-button--small" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F28149981-revolution">Like</a></span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_125824496" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/125824496" />
    <a title="Mariel" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/647547-mariel"><img alt="Mariel" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1451321467p2/647547.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/125824496?book_show_action=true">Oct 11, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mariel" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mariel" href="/user/show/647547-mariel">Mariel</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780385737630" href="/book/show/7558747-revolution">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">my smile is a rifle</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Mariel by: </span>
      children of the revolution
  </div>


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer125824496" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9066552069656039212"><i>"Oh, dead man, you're dead wrong," I tell him. "The world goes on stupid and brutal, but I do not. Can't you see? I do not."<br/></i><br/>That line is the best part of the whole book. The problem with this book is that the ability to understand what message is being told is easier than taking that intimacy inside of you and making it your own heartbreak. You know what they say about forgetting what you learned immediately after the test is over? You didn't really earn it. Experience can beat all, and it doesn</span>
  <span id="freeText9066552069656039212" style="display:none"><i>"Oh, dead man, you're dead wrong," I tell him. "The world goes on stupid and brutal, but I do not. Can't you see? I do not."<br /></i><br />That line is the best part of the whole book. The problem with this book is that the ability to understand what message is being told is easier than taking that intimacy inside of you and making it your own heartbreak. You know what they say about forgetting what you learned immediately after the test is over? You didn't really earn it. Experience can beat all, and it doesn't have to be your own. Some real bodily fluid loving is missing here.<br /><br />I read Jennifer Donnelly's Revolution in mostly one sitting (um bedding) because I'm down with the flu. On a normal health day I might have slugged through it because it's kinda boring in a lacks any urgency sense. I appreciated what Donnelly did with a lot of it, but there's something missing from it. I always felt removed. Maybe I just feel bad already...<br /><br />Teen-aged Andi is prescribed medicated and self-medicated for the past two years of her young life. Picture your stereotypical cynical disaffected youth. Not quite stereotypical, to the credit of Donnelly. The problem was that the storytelling voice relied too much on this disaffectedness (the pretensious art school kids arguing the merits of A Flock of Seagulls made me laugh out loud. Still, who cares if they play dress-up?). I can analyse it and take Andi as more than that, only she sure as hell presents herself that way in the narrative, and at those times I really wanted more. Hers isn't the kind of depression that I can relate to and take inside me, but I can understand it. She blames herself for the death of her beloved brother, Truman. Mom has checked out (and checked into a looney bin), and Dad bailed years before (and not fast like a band aid). It's the feeling of being let down that moved me the most, rather than unimportant relations with her fellow teens (that she cared that the school hated her over the Queen Bitch was silly- enough to leave the country!- considering that it was set up that Andi is beyond caring about that. Huh). The wearing anger to wear I'm not able to get into so much, but the sadness that it's a fact of life her father easily moves on to a new family? It's the doesn't have to force it sadness that was moving. "What is owed me?" by the rest of the world is harder to do. I couldn't get into how easy her new relationship with Virgil is, at least beyond surface stuff of cuteness and liking good music. On paper, I get it that it's easier with those who don't owe you anything (unlike your mom and dad). See, I wish the drugs had been left out of it. The numbness felt more like feeling killing exposition (for this reader) than it did state of being. The drugs come into play when it is time to gloss over the emotions, but doesn't feel like looking up at the world from the bottom of a swimming pool, as these stunting drugs really do. Andi is perpetually suicidal. Yet I never feel the helplessness of that, or her self-hatred. (Not even the reassuring fallback plan kind. Not even cry for help or punishment. It's just delivered information, period.) She doesn't connect to anyone at all apart from knowing her favorite musicians. Andi's favorite music is my favorite music (I have more favorites, of course, but there wasn't one artist mentioned that I don't love to bits). So why does she immediately take to the journal of revolutionary French teenager Alexandrine? There was nothing in those pages that was not (and much, much more) already in the lyrics of her favorite songs (I know because I've heard 'em all). (They sure as shit weren't as good as Morrissey or The Beatles.) I wish I'd felt the connection more than her telling the reader that she was riveted. Or Virgil's cute butt... (who doesn't like a cute butt? Okay...) Too Fred Savage in The Princess Bride enthusiasm for me, before it gets to the "good stuff". (Why do I always think of him?! I think of all telling and not showing as The Wonder Years bad narration. "And we both knew that..." "Really? She doesn't look like she cares.") (I've said this in another gr review, but I'm Kevin Arnold in real life. "yeah, sure" and then overanalysing everything in my head. "Really? He doesn't look like he cares.")<br /><br />Picture it, Sicily. It was 1924 and a beautiful young peasant girl made a wonderful pizza. Her name was... Mama Celeste. Oops, I mean: Picture it, Paris, France. It was 1795 and a plain actor girl had ambitions... She wanted to be Hilary Clinton behind Bill... Whoops, I mean she wanted to charm the young Louis-Charles, and through him the world... Andi feels responsible for the death of her little brother. Alex blames herself for not being able to stop the brutal death of the young prince, whom she grows to love as a brother. It's hard to play the roles you set for yourself, let alone the world wants you to play, and then know how to go on pretending after the worst has happened.<br /><br />When I was about Andi's age I was friends with a depressed Czech Au Pair girl, Lucia. We shared a love of shoe-gazing music and she'd tell me how much she hated watching other people's kids. (I still have some of her mixed tapes. Bands like Ride, Lush, Cranes and Swervedriver are on it. They made her sadder, unlike me, who felt better listening to sad songs.) I have no idea what happened to her. She was really depressed, even more than I was. (The last I heard of her was a post card from home, in 2000. It was of a Madonna and child.) Alexandrine's relationship with the young dauphin reminded me of that, for some reason. Alexandrine's journal is also too much telling. (Donnelly credits actor Gabriel Byrne for answering her questions about acting. I love Gabriel Byrne. That's cool!) I could understand how she wanted to play other parts to be someone else. Like with Andi, it is text book depression and not taking me inside that need to be in another's skin. <br />Anyway, I was listening to Radiohead in those teen years, same as Andi, and I still needed the relating to my friend to understand my own troubles with sadness. I wish I felt it more than that, though... Don't rely on me for this stuff, authors, 'cause I'm still confused.<br /><br />I wanted to high five Andi when she started playing guitar like John Frusciante. I knew she was going to be a fan of his, too. (Probably likes Jim O'rourke too!)<br /><br />Something I felt was to Donnelly's credit was that Andi's being from an affluent family (mama went to the Sorbonne. Dad won a flippin' Nobel) was not an issue. It wasn't even contrasted to Alex's situation in the Revolution. The haves versus the have nots. Something I believe strongly is that it doesn't matter what anybody else has, what anybody else goes through: heartbreak is heartbreak and nobody's negates anybody else's pain. I despise it when people tell you someone else has it worse as if you're supposed to feel smaller (these people always whine endlessly about their own problems, I've noticed). Anyway, I liked that. Not that it didn't bore the shit out of me to read about the rich people. I didn't agree with Alex that no one would want such beauty destroyed. There's beauty everywhere. There's beauty in destruction. It's just not familiar to me, I should say. I can relate to Alex's love of acting and Andi's music. I couldn't relate to feeling owed, or what has to be, other than just wanting emotional well-being.<br /><br />Andi's breaking it down of history for her dad's fancy friends was great. I remember explaining the French revolution to my seventh grade class as this: "They just wanted to turn the tables." <br /><br /><br />They already had it... Sometimes you need the good music to tell you what you already had. Or a long lost journal dealing with the same old shit.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9066552069656039212" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_903321119" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/903321119" />
    <a title="Summer" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14778159-summer"><img alt="Summer" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1574406694p2/14778159.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/903321119?book_show_action=true">Apr 06, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Summer" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Summer" href="/user/show/14778159-summer">Summer</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780385737630" href="/book/show/7558747-revolution">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14778159-summer?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14778159-summer?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14778159-summer?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14778159-summer?shelf=beautiful-writing">beautiful-writing</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer903321119" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12491381504746274349"><blockquote>
  <i>”I am not afraid of beatings or blood anymore. I’m not afraid of guards or guillotines. <br/>There is only one thing I fear now - love. <br/>For I have seen it and I have felt it and I know that it is love, not death, that undoes us.”</i>
</blockquote><br/>Holy shit. What did I just read?<br/><br/><i>Revolution</i> by Jennifer Donnelly goes right up there with novels like <i>I Am the Messenger</i>, <i>A Northern Light</i> (also written by her), and <i>Jellicoe Road</i>. And trust me, I do not honor any book with as prestigious a rank as this. <br/><br/>I really do not kn</span>
  <span id="freeText12491381504746274349" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>”I am not afraid of beatings or blood anymore. I’m not afraid of guards or guillotines. <br />There is only one thing I fear now - love. <br />For I have seen it and I have felt it and I know that it is love, not death, that undoes us.”</i>
</blockquote><br />Holy shit. What did I just read?<br /><br /><i>Revolution</i> by Jennifer Donnelly goes right up there with novels like <i>I Am the Messenger</i>, <i>A Northern Light</i> (also written by her), and <i>Jellicoe Road</i>. And trust me, I do not honor any book with as prestigious a rank as this. <br /><br />I really do not know how I will find the words to describe my endless love for this brilliantly constructed novel, so I will make a list to organize my thoughts - similar to what I did with my review of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1162022.On_the_Jellicoe_Road" title="On the Jellicoe Road by Melina Marchetta" rel="nofollow noopener">On the Jellicoe Road</a>.<br /><br />But first, a bit about the book. The story follows Andi - a music-genius-depression-addled girl, dealing with grief brought on by the death of her younger brother, Truman. Her dad pays little attention to her, or so it seems, and her mother is on the verge of insanity - her paintings the only tether she has. Needless to say, her life kind of sucks. <br /><br />(Fear not, this is not a woe-is-me, plea for sympathy kind of novel. It is much more than that.)<br /><br />In the midst of all this shit, her father decides to embark on a trip to France with Andi. There, she meets a talented rapper (I promise it’s not insta-love!) and a girl named Alexandrine “The Green Man.” I will go no further so as to not spoil the novel.<br /><br /><i>Revolution</i> pretty much has everything I love packed in a 500-page volume. And I enjoyed every damn second of it.<br /><br />So, here are <b>7 Reasons You Should Read Revolution, by Jennifer Donnelly:</b><br /><br /><b>1. THE HISTORY.</b> <br /><br />Very well researched, which equals a happy Summer. When it comes to history, I am a full-fledged dork. Obviously. <br /><br />This is more than a recount of the French Rev; no, it is much more personal than that. We are plopped smack in the middle of the streets of Paris alongside Alexandrine, an ambitious actress. There are multiple appearances by many influential historical figures, which I’m sure will make any history lover giddy. <br /><br />Not to spoil anything, but my previous views of the Royalists and the Revolutionaries (particularly the Jacobins) have been blurred.<br /><br /><b>2. THE CHARACTERS.</b> <br /><br />Nathan, Virgil, G., Lilli, Vijay - all characters I absolutely adore. Did I already say Donnelly has mastered the art of character development? This is also true for her previous YA novel, <i>A Northern Light</i>. <br /><br />And I don’t think I’ll ever forget the protagonist, Andi, anytime soon. At first I thought she was an insufferable bitch, but within a few pages my perception of her was completely flipped. She became my best friend; I felt as if I was right next to her, experiencing her experiences and feeling her emotions, and my love for her grew by the page. <br /><br />I’m a bit annoyed, though, by the mostly male cast of characters, but I’m able to let it slide.<br /><br /><b>3. THE FEELS &amp; WRITING.</b><br /><blockquote>
  <i>”I don’t like hope very much. In fact, I hate it. It’s the crystal meth of emotions. It hooks you fast and kills you hard. It’s bad news. The worst. It’s sharp sticks and cherry bombs. When hope shows up, it’s only a matter of time until someone gets hurt.”</i>
</blockquote><br />Counting how many times I <s>full-on</s> almost cried in <i>Revolution</i> would be pointless. Whether it was about Louis Charles or Truman or even music I found myself tearing up. I haven’t been this emotionally affected since, well, last year. <br /><br />The writing was impeccable, typical Donnelly. I can still hear Andi’s voice in my head; the author has just captured the protagonist’s voice <i>that well.</i><br /><br />(Side note: This is the third book I've given 5 stars this year. Yup, it’s that good.)<br /><br /><b>4. THE DOSE OF CONTEMPORARY.</b> <s>Pun intended.</s> <br /><br />If you’re more of a contemporary type of gal/guy, do not worry. Tackled in this coming-of-age novel include drugs, suicide, racism, and death. It’s a pretty bleak novel, as you can tell, so don’t expect an uplifting sort of tale. <br /><br />Actually, very normal topics are brought in alongside the grim ones. Andi is just trying to survive her senior year of high school, and at the start of the novel, she is failing all her classes, despite her history of straight-As. This isn't a full-on historical fiction novel; it’s quite eclectic. <br /><br /><b>5. THE MUSIC.</b> <br /><br />I’m not much of a musician, but I do thoroughly enjoy music. Virgil’s rap scenes were some of my favorites, and envisioning him rapping on stage made him 10x hotter. Sad truth: I sometimes skim and at times entirely skip poem and lyric segments in a book; this was not the case in <i>Revolution.</i> Furthermore, some of the most beautiful descriptions in this novel were of music and Andi’s intense love for it. Being the total n00b I am, I Googled “Malherbeau,” thinking he was some obscure musician. Apparently, he’s not real. *sad face*<br /><br /><b>6. THE ADVENTURE.</b> (read: <b>TIME TRAVEL OMG</b>) <br /><br />Again, I won’t expand on this much because I don’t want to ruin it for those who haven’t read this. But, I’ll just say that there is a ton of fireworks and sneaking and other fun stuff.<br /><br /><b>7. THE SCIENCE.</b> <br /><br />If you’re neither a contemporary nor a history buff, there is plenty of science, particularly genetics and DNA. It was quite fascinating when Andi’s dad was talking about the methods they used to uncover the mystery of Louis-Charles. The debate of Science vs. History was intriguing, and I don’t think I need to explicitly say which side I supported. <br /><br />Donnelly provides an alternate view to the French Revolution - one that is both thought-provoking and downright brilliant. An intricate story that has permanently found its spot on my favorites list. </span>
  <a data-text-id="12491381504746274349" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3513963381?book_show_action=true">Aug 26, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title=" LEAH⇢" class="user" itemprop="url" name=" LEAH⇢" href="/user/show/9683519-leah"> LEAH⇢</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/26918181-revolution">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9683519-leah?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9683519-leah?shelf=listened-on-audio">listened-on-audio</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9683519-leah?shelf=historical">historical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9683519-leah?shelf=ya-ish">ya-ish</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9683519-leah?shelf=read-2020">read-2020</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9683519-leah?shelf=musically-influenced">musically-influenced</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9683519-leah?shelf=splash-of-romance">splash-of-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9683519-leah?shelf=time-travel">time-travel</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3513963381" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11599373995471317041"><b>THE DETAILS✎</b> <i>❐ 4¼ STARS ❐ PARIS SETTING BOTH 1790'S AND PRESENT DAY-ISH ❐ DUAL POV'S --ONE PRESENT (ANDI) & ONE PAST (ALEX) ❐ A SENIOR THESIS PROJECT ❐ FRENCH REVOLUTION ❐ MUSICALLY INFLUENCED BOTH MODERN & CLASSICAL ❐ TIME-TRAVELING OR JUST A REALLY VIVID DREAMSCAPE ❐ LENGTH OF AUDIO ➯ 15 HOURS, 4 MINUTES ❐ I LISTENED ON LIBBY THROUGH MY LIBRARY</i><br/><blockquote>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1598852626i/30039145._SY540_.jpg' width='410' height='350' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</blockquote><br/><br/>MY REVIEW IN ONE SENTENCE ➯ A historical story immersed within a modern story with a dollop of romance, plenty of music references, time-travel, and</span>
  <span id="freeText11599373995471317041" style="display:none"><b>THE DETAILS✎</b> <i>❐ 4¼ STARS ❐ PARIS SETTING BOTH 1790'S AND PRESENT DAY-ISH ❐ DUAL POV'S --ONE PRESENT (ANDI) &amp; ONE PAST (ALEX) ❐ A SENIOR THESIS PROJECT ❐ FRENCH REVOLUTION ❐ MUSICALLY INFLUENCED BOTH MODERN &amp; CLASSICAL ❐ TIME-TRAVELING OR JUST A REALLY VIVID DREAMSCAPE ❐ LENGTH OF AUDIO ➯ 15 HOURS, 4 MINUTES ❐ I LISTENED ON LIBBY THROUGH MY LIBRARY</i><br><blockquote>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1598852626i/30039145._SY540_.jpg" width="410" height="350" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</blockquote><br><br>MY REVIEW IN ONE SENTENCE ➯ A historical story immersed within a modern story with a dollop of romance, plenty of music references, time-travel, and one broken family trying to cope with the pain of losing someone they love.<br><br>The narration by Emily Janice Card &amp; Emma Bering was very well performed. I did struggle sometimes with comprehending the french words and accents, but that's on me. It's funny though after I finished this and went to sleep, throughout my dreams I kept hearing french accents.<br><br>This started out slow...with a lot of inane teen drama and chatter...but once the MC goes to Paris with her Dad...things get a whole lot more interesting. It was like a history lesson on the French Revolution with a bonus of music history. I really enjoyed this aspect and even tried to look up the composer that she was doing her thesis on...but alas, I think he was made up.<br><br>There is some time-traveling of a sort, which for others could be a turn-off, but it really only enhanced the history aspect for me and I really liked it. Overall, I found this to be an entertaining story, and since the narration was so excellently performed I readily recommend the audio version...especially for those slow parts of the story...listening always makes this so much easier to power through than actual reading. <br><br><br><b>BREAKDOWN✎</b><br><i>Narration ➯ 5 STARS<br>Plot ➯ 4.3/5<br>Characters ➯ 4/5<br>The Feels ➯ 4.3/5<br>Pacing ➯ 4/5<br>Addictiveness ➯ 4.3/5<br>Theme, Tone or Intensity ➯ 4.3/5<br>Originality ➯ 5/5<br>Flow (Writing Style/Ease of Listening) ➯ 4.2/5<br>World-Building ➯ 4.3/5<br>Ending ➯ 5/5<br>SUMMATION ➯ 4¼ STARS</i><br><br><blockquote>

    <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1579478819i/28807604.png" width="300" height="65" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
</blockquote></span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_117322512" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/117322512" />
    <a title="Becky" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1376766-becky"><img alt="Becky" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582132250p2/1376766.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/117322512?book_show_action=true">Aug 17, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Becky" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Becky" href="/user/show/1376766-becky">Becky</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780385737630" href="/book/show/7558747-revolution">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=2010">2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=mystery-and-thrillers">mystery-and-thrillers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=multi-dimensional">multi-dimensional</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=highly-recommended">highly-recommended</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=bad-shit-and-atrocities">bad-shit-and-atrocities</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=romance-y">romance-y</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=review-copies">review-copies</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=politicalish">politicalish</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer117322512" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13188443799415948135">This is the second of Donnelly's books that I've read, the first being <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/64481.A_Northern_Light' title='A Northern Light by Jennifer Donnelly' rel='nofollow noopener'>A Northern Light</a> (or if you're in the UK, "A Gathering Light") which I loved. I loved the wordplay and the characters and the story... it was just beautiful to me, with a bit of innocence almost. <br/><br/>This story is nothing like that, but if anything, I like it more for it. There are some similarities between the two stories, though. Each features a girl who stumbles upon a link to the past that is surrounded by mystery. Each featu</span>
  <span id="freeText13188443799415948135" style="display:none">This is the second of Donnelly's books that I've read, the first being <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/64481.A_Northern_Light" title="A Northern Light by Jennifer Donnelly" rel="nofollow noopener">A Northern Light</a> (or if you're in the UK, "A Gathering Light") which I loved. I loved the wordplay and the characters and the story... it was just beautiful to me, with a bit of innocence almost. <br /><br />This story is nothing like that, but if anything, I like it more for it. There are some similarities between the two stories, though. Each features a girl who stumbles upon a link to the past that is surrounded by mystery. Each features a girl struggling to find herself and happiness against all odds. And each features a girl who shares an intense love of something with a boy who understands that love completely. In "A Northern Light" it was words and language and writing, and in "Revolution" it is music. <br /><br />It seems to me that lately there have been a lot of new books, particularly YA books, which feature music in such a way that it is almost an extension of the character as well as a character itself. Music featured as not only something to enjoy, but as a necessary component to life, like water or air or food. <br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/4374400.If_I_Stay" title="If I Stay by Gayle Forman" rel="nofollow noopener">If I Stay</a> by Gayle Forman is one of these books, as is <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6454183.Harmonic_Feedback" title="Harmonic Feedback by Tara Kelly" rel="nofollow noopener">Harmonic Feedback</a> by Tara Kelly (although I've only discussed this book with a friend so far, I haven't read it myself), and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6587879.Horns" title="Horns by Joe Hill" rel="nofollow noopener">Horns</a> by Joe Hill, which is not YA, but features music in the way I'm talking about. These books show beautifully how important music is as a method of communication, as art, as life. <br /><br />"Revolution" is no different in that aspect. The main character, Andi, is in pain due to the death of her brother, and nothing helps except for music. It's her lifeline, her one passion, her air. Without it she has nothing and no reason to go on from day to day. But it's more than just a life-preserver, it's who she is. I'm a reader. I can't pass a word without reading it. Andi is a musician. She finds music in everything, and feels and understands music in a way that most people probably never will. <br /><br />When she's in danger of flunking out of school and of not graduating, her absentee father makes her go with him to Paris, thinking that the change of scenery would give her a new outlook and help her to focus. While there, she begins work on her thesis, which is about the composer Amade Malherbeau and how his work has influenced music to this day, and during the course of that research, she stumbles on a mystery that goes all the way back to Revolutionary France.<br /><br />I don't want you to think that this book is only about music, because it is not. It's about so much more. It's about understanding who we are, and where we came from. It's about heeding our past to prevent it from recurring. It's about making mistakes and surviving them. It's about being willing to give everything for what you believe in, even if it we don't succeed. It's about learning to live again. It's about the parallels between the past and the present. It's about the value of someone who takes the time to care and be there for someone who needs it. It's about all of these things and more. <br /><br />This is a beautiful, layered, and intricate story that I could not stop thinking about. When I wasn't reading it, I wanted to be. It seemed to suck me in almost from the very first page. I wanted to know more about Andi, and why she is hurting as badly as she is, what makes her so jaded and bitter and angry. I hoped for her to find that something in life that makes it worth holding on to. <br /><br />There's a running theme in the story of being haunted by our pasts, both in the present day story line and the Revolutionary story line. It reminds me of a song by Paramore, off of their "Brand New Eyes" album. It's a beautiful song, and I think it fits the story as well, especially considering the music theme. <br /><br />If you'd like to hear it, here's a link to a YouTube video. <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=YP53i8Md02c">http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=YP53i8...</a> <br /><br /><i><b>Misguided Ghosts by Paramore:</b><br /><br />I am going away for a while<br />But I'll be back, don't try and follow me<br />'Cause I'll return as soon as possible<br />See I'm trying to find my place<br />But it might not be here where I feel safe<br />We all learn to make mistakes<br /><br />And run<br />From them, from them<br />With no direction<br />We'll run from them, from them<br />With no conviction<br /><br />'Cause I'm just one of those ghosts<br />Traveling endlessly<br />Don't need no roads<br />In fact they follow me<br /><br />And we just go in circles<br /><br />Well now I'm told that this is life<br />And pain is just a simple compromise<br />So we can get what we want out of it<br />Would someone care to classify,<br />Of broken hearts and twisted minds<br />So I can find someone to rely on<br /><br />And run<br />To them, to them<br />Full speed ahead<br />Oh you are not useless<br />We are just<br /><br />Misguided ghosts<br />Traveling endlessly<br />The ones we trusted the most<br />Pushed us far away<br />And there's no one road<br />We should not be the same<br />But I'm just a ghost<br />And still they echo me<br /><br />They echo me in circles</i><br /><br />Overall, I loved the story. I loved the dual storylines, and the parallels and the small details that Donnelly included that made the story that much more tangible. I highly recommend this one. </span>
  <a data-text-id="13188443799415948135" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
